  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3ab80560-0165-4d12-8374-e88eeb97262f'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">*spoiler* The main character were in love with Finn but to afraid to say something (and vise versa). They were with other people because they were att<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">*spoiler* The main character were in love with Finn but to afraid to say something (and vise versa). They were with other people because they were attracted to them and even came to love them, but Autumn and Finn's hearts were still set to each other.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div id="review_421658564" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/421658564" />
    <a title="Jasprit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4841793-jasprit"><img alt="Jasprit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456315622p2/4841793.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/421658564?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasprit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasprit" href="/user/show/4841793-jasprit">Jasprit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=out-2013">out-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=arc-galley">arc-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=love-the-cover">love-the-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer421658564" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10107758202722955217">If He Had Been With Me was a poignant story which I devoured in one sitting. It’s a story which deals with issues of friendship, first loves and family in the most raw and intense way I have come across in a long time. It was a story which I knew how would end, but I was utterly mesmerised into reading because of the beautiful heart rendering prose.<br/><br/>The story opens with the most heart breaking chapter, it gives you an insight into how things end. Despite knowing this I continually tried to bury t</span>
  <span id="freeText10107758202722955217" style="display:none">If He Had Been With Me was a poignant story which I devoured in one sitting. It’s a story which deals with issues of friendship, first loves and family in the most raw and intense way I have come across in a long time. It was a story which I knew how would end, but I was utterly mesmerised into reading because of the beautiful heart rendering prose.<br /><br />The story opens with the most heart breaking chapter, it gives you an insight into how things end. Despite knowing this I continually tried to bury this awful fact at the back of my mind, I kept trying to make myself believe that the author would change the course of the story and that maybe she was just playing with us. So it came as no surprise that when the ending did finally come, I found myself choked up all over again.<br /><br />If He Had Been With Me deals with the story of what ifs. Autumn and Finn had been best friends forever, they did everything together, until middle school, that they fell apart for some reason or another. Despite their mothers being best friends, and being neighbours, there was always that awkward tension between them when they spent “family time” together. Also they hung out with friends who were on opposite sides of the spectrum to one another, so were seen to never mix or interact with one another. Despite having a great set of friends and boyfriend in Jamie, Autumn’s regret over the loss of her friendship with Finn is clearly apparent. At first it’s like a niggling at the back of her mind, which she continues to throw away and just focus on the good things happening in her life at the moment, but the further she goes through school and seeing Finn all the time bring several feelings of anger, betrayal, love, and loneliness which are continuously eating away at her until it all becomes too much. What would have happened if Autumn and Finn didn’t grow apart? Would things have been different now? It’s these constant thoughts that Autumn can’t shut away.<br /><br />The Story is told with flash backs into Autumn’s and Finn’s memories when they were younger alongside Autumn’s current progression in school, some readers may find confusing. But I thought these alternating changes in the time span worked wonderfully. The stories were timed right as to show their significance into why that memory had a specific impact to why Autumn was the way she was today. It gave a better understanding into Autumn’s character, and a connection between her in a deep and meaningful way. Some readers may have got frustrated with Autumn’s decisions, but if I were in her shoes I don’t think I would have done it any other way. She had to battle through a lot in this story, and I think she dealt with it the best way she could.<br /><br />Nowlin focused on many dark and tough issues in this story, issues of depression, family problems and loneliness were explored in depth. What made these issues more realistic was that they weren’t just touched upon once, but they were followed upon Autumn’s progression through school and clearly showed an important part of the type of person Autumn became. I liked how despite their differences Finn was the one who could constantly ground Autumn, the one she could turn to when she needed the most. Her friends were also a supportive bunch, and I enjoyed the fun they had and the time they spent together, but one particular point which I didn’t expect at all, blemished my high opinion I held of some of them.<br /><br />If you’re worried about giving this book a try because of the heart breaking story please don’t because Nowlin’s gorgeous prose is not one to be missed. Her writing was littered with several beautiful passages and was delicate yet purposeful with each word puncturing a hole in my heart. Despite being a complete mess a few days afterwards and constantly asking myself how and why Nowlin would do this to me. I am sure that He Had Been With Me will remain as one of my favourites reads for a long time to come.<br /><br />My feelings for this book are perfectly summed up by this gorgeous quote from this book:<br /><br /><i>“This book is a treasure; I did not suspect it would be so good when I picked it up, but now I can feel the printed words seeping through my skin and into my veins, rushing to my heart and marking it forever. I want to savour this wonder, this happening of a loving book and reading it for the first time, because the first time is always the best, and I will never read this book for the first time again”</i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10107758202722955217" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8632292406600409397">Wow. I did not expected it to be this good. Damn you Laura Nowlin! I will stalk you till you give me a new book! <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380392752i/756113.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>If He Had Been With Me was on my 'can't wait' list for months and I couldn't resist and read it the moment I got my hands on it.   <span id="freeText8632292406600409397" style="display:none">Wow. I did not expected it to be this good. Damn you Laura Nowlin! I will stalk you till you give me a new book! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380392752i/756113.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If He Had Been With Me was on my 'can't wait' list for months and I couldn't resist and read it the moment I got my hands on it. I started reading in the morning and didn't put it down until I was done crying because I had a feeling someone stabbed me in the heart even though the book started with the most unpleasant thing than can happen. I chose to ignore it. There was just no way the story would go there. Well, I cried for a long time. <br><br>Autumn used to be friends with her first door neighbor, Finn but after middle school she becomes very popular and they grow apart. Now in high school, Autumn is a part of a gang who are different from other students. They dress differently, listen to cool music, change their hair colors, well you get the picture. Finn is hangin with the popular crowd-cheerleaders and football players and they ignore each other all the time except it's hard since their mothers are really close friends and they even eat together. <br><br>Even though Finn and Autumn are not friends any more she can help but think about the time they spent together so we get to read about their childhood memories. Finn is such a sweet guy and is a devoted friend so I couldn't help but cheer for him to end up with Autumn even though they were both dating other people. Autumn is also battling with depression which she ignores as a winter blues. Her boyfriend is not really helpful in that department so Finn is there to make it all better. Finn's dad is also never around but he tries to buy his affection with expensive gifts. Both characters need each other to move on from their issues but disaster strikes and everything changes. <br><br>I love to read heartbreaking stories because they make me feel alive. Make me see life in another light. I will bore my friends to pick this book up until they block me. I urge you to buy it. It's worth the money. Yes! I know you want to read it. So what are you waiting for? </span>

        <a title="Hannah ◇Reader in the Rough◇" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah ◇Reader in the Rough◇" href="/user/show/42354688-hannah-reader-in-the-rough">Hannah ◇Reader in the Rough◇</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1287228939" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7475729510145824069"><i>"Perhaps he would ask me what books mean to me. I would tell him that it means living another life." </i><br/><br/>This book was so uncomfortable to read. The metamorphosis of Autumn runs parallel to my own teen years. <br/><br/>This book didn't feel like another life, <b> it felt like an alternate universe of my own. </b> Not because I had a boyfriend I didn't appreciate, or a boy that I loved and didn't deserve.<u> Because I asked the same questions, showered until I was numb, craved books because I couldn't stand my own actio</u></span>
  <span id="freeText7475729510145824069" style="display:none"><i>"Perhaps he would ask me what books mean to me. I would tell him that it means living another life." </i><br /><br />This book was so uncomfortable to read. The metamorphosis of Autumn runs parallel to my own teen years. <br /><br />This book didn't feel like another life, <b> it felt like an alternate universe of my own. </b> Not because I had a boyfriend I didn't appreciate, or a boy that I loved and didn't deserve.<u> Because I asked the same questions, showered until I was numb, craved books because I couldn't stand my own actions in a blurry and unforgiving world, and feared I was on the path to being trapped in my own mind like my couch-ridden mother. </u><br /><br /><i>
  <b>“I can see some of the roses still blooming in my mother´s garden. Brown on the edges and bright in other colors, their petals drooping downward, dying just as their lives have begun."</b>
</i><br /><br />You know where the story will end with the never-ending sense of dread in Autumn's narrative; it's no surprise. But what may surprise you is that <b> part of you goes down this rabbit hole, welling up newfound regret, breathing in anger at the fucked-up world that honestly doesn't get better as you get older. You learn to cope and to harden, to get over it and care less. The past is over and you can't do anything about it, so just <u> keep moving</u>. </b>Right?<br /><br />Autumn doesn't. That is mental illness: <b>the constant rewind and fast forward of feeling too much and not enough, the past being as palpable as the present. </b><br /><br />This is one of the most real and painfully beautiful teen contemporaries I have read.<br /> <br /><i>"I can feel the printed words seeping through my skin and into my veins, rushing to my heart and marking it forever." </i><br /><br /><b>Lay your fingers on this thorny rose of a book.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="7475729510145824069" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_530847396" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/530847396" />
    <a title="Nomes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3842653-nomes"><img alt="Nomes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499148999p2/3842653.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/530847396?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nomes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nomes" href="/user/show/3842653-nomes">Nomes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=tissue-box-books">tissue-box-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=love-the-premise">love-the-premise</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=my-kind-of-awesome">my-kind-of-awesome</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=swoon">swoon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=themes-i-love">themes-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=you-make-me-smile">you-make-me-smile</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=crushing-on-the-writing">crushing-on-the-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=i-had-no-idea-i-would-love-this-so">i-had-no-idea-i-would-love-this-so</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer530847396" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10901415846246166575">It has been a long time since I have fallen so hard for a contemporary YA novel. I have barely heard of any buzz surrounding Laura Nowlin's debut. I ordered it on a whim, not really sure what to expect. I liked the cover, the premise sounded like my kind of thing and I always like the chase of finding a YA book free of preconceived hopes and praise. <br/><br/>I was unprepared for just <i> how good </i> this book is, easily my favourite YA book of the year so far and it now sits on my favourites shelf.<br/><br/>Nowlin is a</span>
  <span id="freeText10901415846246166575" style="display:none">It has been a long time since I have fallen so hard for a contemporary YA novel. I have barely heard of any buzz surrounding Laura Nowlin's debut. I ordered it on a whim, not really sure what to expect. I liked the cover, the premise sounded like my kind of thing and I always like the chase of finding a YA book free of preconceived hopes and praise. <br /><br />I was unprepared for just <i> how good </i> this book is, easily my favourite YA book of the year so far and it now sits on my favourites shelf.<br /><br />Nowlin is a born storyteller. And this book differs from other YA books as it spans over three years of Autumn's life (told in the present, but it also encapsulated much more than that with memories and flashbacks). I love the time span of this novel, it stretched ahead of me and wrapped itself around me and I was entirely absorbed into Autumn's world.<br /><br />This is a YA coming-of-age love story, but not in that swoony, predictable way. It hit me harder than a just the regular dreamy smile for the hot guy next door (and Finny is a hot boy living next door): I felt it right through to my stomach and to my chest constricting as I watched August and Finny together. The things left unsaid, the memories swirling around them, hope's dashed, future's uncertain. <br /><br />Nowlin so perfectly captures that teen voice: the misunderstandings between teenagers, the things unsaid, the dreams, the doubts, the wildly good times and also snatches of depression. I love Autumn as she felt so real. no aspect of her was gimmicky. She was fully nuanced, so gorgeous and bold and different without ever falling into a YA cliché and I loved seeing the world from her eyes. She was the perfect blend of confident and unsure. Nothing was black and white: I loved all the shades of grey in her feelings and everything that was going on in her world. I loved her for her fairytale hopes all mashed up with trying to face reality. For her love of reading and her uncompromising stance on who she was, even as she was trying to figure out the very same thing. <br /><br />And, oh, how I love the history of her relationship with Finny. There are a lot of flashbacks and memories and I never grew tired of it. I felt included in their lives. Finny himself is now one of my most favourite YA boys, not just as a gorgeous love interest, but for who he was. <br /><br />If He Had Been With Me has it's own unique vibe. The prose sometimes has it's own jaunty little rhythm, other times passages are so so poignant and heartfelt that my chest constricted. The writing was deeply personal, holding nothing back. <br /><br />With such a lush scope of three years plus, Nowlin explores so many experiences: friendships, cliques, first love, divorce, mental health, sex, all those gorgeous moments caught between the mystery and promise of adulthood looming ahead while thinking back on childhood. <br /><br />The thing about this book is it just kept getting better and better. For me, it was like meeting a new friend, and liking them, and then getting to know them until they become one of those lifelong besties that you cannot imagine life without. I liked Autumn so much from the outset, but she grew on me, exponentially so, as did her friends, her mum (and aunty) and, of course, Finny and now I just have this love for them and I know I won't ever be forgetting this gorgeous, beautiful and achey story. <br /><br />For discussion: I would have preferred the book without the prologue chapter. The writing itself pulled me into the story, that and the promise of what was to come - I did not need such a dramatic hook. I also am not a fan of the blurb that's on GR. I think it changes the reading experience (luckily, I did not read the blurb on that site - which is also used on most bloggers review posts, amazon, etc - and only read the back cover of the book). The ending felt rushed, then abrupt. I think I needed a tiny bit longer to linger in the story, to make sense of it all, but I understand what Nowlin was trying to do. <br /><br />I can't stop thinking about this story. I am crazily excited to fall this hard for a debut author and cannot wait to read more of Nowlin's work (understatement). I have a new absolute favourite book, so much passages bookmarked. I have so much love for this book and hope it falls into many hands. I envy those readers their first time reading experience waiting before them. LOVE<br /><br />(Confession: I stayed up until 4.30am to finish this one. My only regret is it's already over...)<br /><br />Perfect theme song: the Special Two by the ever lush Missy Higgins<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PJA92W-2dzU">http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PJA92W...</a><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10901415846246166575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/445824006?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer445824006" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9062445241714235476">This book could have been epic... <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/553731.gif' width='240' height='275' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The beautiful cover and the description of this book lured me in and I couldn’t wait to read this story. I knew from the description, that a tragedy would occur. I was more than prepared to take the journey and meet Autumn and Finny. The part that I wasn’t prepared for was the abrupt anticlimactic ending. <br/> <br/>The story brings a reader through four years of high school with the back ground of Finn and Autumn’s neighbor/best friend/family relationship that has now be</span>
  <span id="freeText9062445241714235476" style="display:none">This book could have been epic... <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/553731.gif" width="240" height="275" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The beautiful cover and the description of this book lured me in and I couldn’t wait to read this story. I knew from the description, that a tragedy would occur. I was more than prepared to take the journey and meet Autumn and Finny. The part that I wasn’t prepared for was the abrupt anticlimactic ending. <br> <br>The story brings a reader through four years of high school with the back ground of Finn and Autumn’s neighbor/best friend/family relationship that has now become strained while both characters find themselves and pursue different friends.<br><br>I would rate the majority of the book as a <b>4 star</b> read. I loved following Autumn’s teenage life, friends, family and boyfriends. Sadly, I would have to give the ending a <b>1 star</b> rating. <br><br>As a reader the story’s slow build up to Autumn and Finny declaring their love which does finally occurs in the last 90% of the book. However, the whole thing falls apart in the last couple of pages with an abrupt weak ending. <br><br>There were no surprises found in the ending, no profound moments, nothing, NADA.<br><br>Overall, I loved Autumn and Finny and felt deflated not sad by the end of the book. I wanted so much more for our main character.</span>

  <span id="freeText14060376638430444562" style="display:none"><br><b> IF:</b><br><br><i> The saddest word in the English dictionary.</i><br><br>Okay...<br><br>No, wait. I'm not okay.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447695716ra/17038808.gif" width="500" height="381" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>If there's one thing that I can proudly say about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15835031.If_He_Had_Been_with_Me" title="If He Had Been with Me by Laura Nowlin" rel="nofollow noopener">If He Had Been with Me</a>, it's that it can make you sad. I wouldn't normally like this book because <i>"bestfriends, highschool, drama and first love"</i> are the key words that let me know that I will soon be frustrated with what I am reading.<br><br>But that was not the case with this book.<br><br>I love this. I devoured it in one sitting and though it didn't shatter my already cynical heart, it did cracked it. I think that the most powerful thing that this book can give you is the feeling of regret and God knows though I never had a lot of things in my life that I regretted , it still makes me fucking sad.<br><br>And to quote what Autumn said, <b>"Being sad is beautiful.</b><br><br>And so is this book.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer981664550" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15366333439529179283"><b>Actual Rating: 2.5/5 stars</b><br/><br/>I was actually enjoying this book despite it's not very unique storyline. I cared about the characters. The romance was SO good that this book could've been a new favorite of mine but..<br/><br/>The ending just ruined everything, really. For me, anyway. I wished I didn't read that part.<br/><br/><b>The plot:</b><br/><br/>Autumn and Finny are best friends since birth, literally. "The Mothers", as they call them, are also best friends so they were with each other before they're even born. As they grew up, th</span>
  <span id="freeText15366333439529179283" style="display:none"><b>Actual Rating: 2.5/5 stars</b><br /><br />I was actually enjoying this book despite it's not very unique storyline. I cared about the characters. The romance was SO good that this book could've been a new favorite of mine but..<br /><br />The ending just ruined everything, really. For me, anyway. I wished I didn't read that part.<br /><br /><b>The plot:</b><br /><br />Autumn and Finny are best friends since birth, literally. "The Mothers", as they call them, are also best friends so they were with each other before they're even born. As they grew up, they drift apart though. <br /><br /><i>Who doesn't like best friends who became more than that? </i><b>That is the best kind of love story.</b> For me, anyway. Having someone you already trusts to to take care of you is comforting. And even after all romance is gone, friendship is all you have.<br /><br />Autumn and Finny were both in a relationship with other people. But throughout the entire story, I just wished that they should be together. The author made me feel that they belonged together like it's a universal accepted truth. <br /><br />There are parts that had me completely bored though. Some scenes just does not fit like they should not be there at all. And this was just so loooooong.<br /><br /><b>The Characters:</b><br /><br /><b>Autumn. </b>I liked her. She was weird and she knows it AND embraces it. She is so geeky and I liked that she reads a lot. I like that there's actually school activities going on here. She's pretty active in recitation.<br /><br />I just don't liked what she did at the end. It was seriously infuriating and sad at the same time. <br /><br /><b>Finny.</b> I adore him. He blushed so easily when he's embarassed which I found cute. What are you, blind Autumn? It was so obvious that he liked her! This MC is just ao dense sometimes I want to strangle her. <br /><br />I wished I knew what Finny thinks most of the time. It would be good to read something from his POV. The thing that happened before that horrible ending is perfect. I was genuinely happy for them. I mean, finally!! <br /><br /><b>The Ending:</b><br /><br />Are you kidding me???<i> I am completely and utterly furious! </i>My heart aches at the same time though. I feel like being punched in the gut after what happened in the end but the author made me so angry shortly after that.<br /><br />The book just ended suddenly. I don't like this kind of ending! I have so many questions but this book just left more questions unanswered. I was definitely not okay with it. I know that a tragedy would happen as the blurb says and I was prepared! But that ending? Gaaah.<br /><br />Overall, an okay contemporary romance with a bad ending. I don't know if I recommend it. Maybe not.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15366333439529179283" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_584250271" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/584250271" />
    <a title="Ceecee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10394610-ceecee"><img alt="Ceecee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456943309p2/10394610.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/584250271?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ceecee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ceecee" href="/user/show/10394610-ceecee">Ceecee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10394610-ceecee?shelf=fictional-boyfriends">fictional-boyfriends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10394610-ceecee?shelf=2-star">2-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10394610-ceecee?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer584250271" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4258779165115981637">It's almost 3AM and I am reeling from my reading experience. <i>How to even begin?</i><br/><br/>Last I left the book I was more than halfway through. I thought I could definitely finish this "tomorrow", but I meant like tomorrow afternoon. Well it literally is "tomorrow" since it's the 13th of April. 3AM. <br/><br/>So since it's apparently hard to put down (it's really easy to read), why do I only want to rate this 2 stars? Well, 2.5 stars. 2 stars means it was okay. I had such good hopes for this. I actually felt like I </span>
  <span id="freeText4258779165115981637" style="display:none">It's almost 3AM and I am reeling from my reading experience. <i>How to even begin?</i><br /><br />Last I left the book I was more than halfway through. I thought I could definitely finish this "tomorrow", but I meant like tomorrow afternoon. Well it literally is "tomorrow" since it's the 13th of April. 3AM. <br /><br />So since it's apparently hard to put down (it's really easy to read), why do I only want to rate this 2 stars? Well, 2.5 stars. 2 stars means it was okay. I had such good hopes for this. I actually felt like I could like this, and now I feel bad for not. <br /><br />Like most books I've read, the final impression it leaves me determines my overall impression of the book. *Sigh* <b>Now I must warn you that there may be spoilers ahead</b>. Most likely. Obviously I can't write properly since it's 3AM and I'm running on adrenaline here, and a famous writer once said:<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>I believe that words uttered in passion contain a greater living truth than do those words which express thoughts rationally conceived. -Natsume Soseki,<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/762476.Kokoro" title="Kokoro by Sōseki Natsume" rel="nofollow noopener">Kokoro</a> </blockquote>
</i><br /><br />So here goes nothing:<br /><br />I really liked how this novel was realistic, and made you care about the story despite its simplicity. I may not have had the same experiences as Autumn had in highschool, but <b>the novel rings true</b>. Not everyone can be perfect, nor make the choices that an outsider [read: reader] would choose, nor do things that we all expect. Autumn and Finny, from the outset, <b>you knew that they belonged together</b>. You're reading it to know why and how they are not.<br /><br />And then the book was an almost detailed account of their high school life. Autumn started dating this guy and Finn dates this girl in their freshman year. It wasn't like old times, and they seem to have grown apart. But you see, Autumn is such an unreliable narrator, even though she says Finn and her are no longer friends, you can read between the lines: that they have sexual tension, and Autumn is an idiot. <br /><br />What I cannot like is how the story seemed so stagnant. A lot has happened, but not much essential to the story. I loved getting frustrated when I realize what Finny really felt in this scene and that, and I liked Autumn sometimes. Who doesn't often feel like they're dreams and reality can't coincide? So what if Autumn chooses to have a stable life with James instead of pursuing her love with Finn? We're all idiots. And I'm okay with that.<br /><br />What I'm not okay with is how there didn't seem to be character development. Especially with that ending. <b>Is this frigging City of Angels?</b> The two protagonists spend <b>one bloody day</b> together after confessing and consummating their great love, and are separated forever the next day? Why would Laura Nowlin do this to me? And Autumn's reaction? She'll think Finny would forgive her for that? I never really took her seriously when she said Romeo and Juliet was romantic, because hell I liked Romeo and Juliet and sure it was romantic, but <b>there's fiction and there's reality</b>. So when Autumn decided to follow Finny into the dark, I think that was poor character development. What's more, she decides to do it again until she succeeds. *facepalm* Is it really nice to present in a novel that a girl is so devastated in love she wants to kill herself, because there's nothing else to live for? But oh wait, she's pregnant, and she thinks about aborting it, but the thought of Finny stops her. It would have been so nice if she had made a decision because that's what <i>she</i> stands up for, and not merely for the sake of a departed love.<br /><br /><b>*2.5 stars</b> </span>
  <a data-text-id="4258779165115981637" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16699933781201809488" style="display:none">Reading this book was like listening most hauntingly beautiful and sad song. <div id="review_476810581" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/476810581" />
    <a title="Joy (joyous reads)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4352734-joy-joyous-reads"><img alt="Joy (joyous reads)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1526951297p2/4352734.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/476810581?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joy (joyous reads)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joy (joyous reads)" href="/user/show/4352734-joy-joyous-reads">Joy (joyous reads)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Joy (joyous reads) by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4841793-jasprit">Jasprit</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4352734-joy-joyous-reads?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4352734-joy-joyous-reads?shelf=cant-put-these-down">cant-put-these-down</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer476810581" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18156317230361933182">Whenever I pick up a novel, I dive head first hopeful that the characters will have their happily ever afters. I picture their romance in my head like an endless reel of a silent movie: their first meeting will be perfectly awkward and the relationship to happen in a slow but realistic build-up that would have me anticipating and salivating for their fruition. But when the two characters wasn't really working so good for me, I'd also find myself wishing that they don't get together at all. This </span>
  <span id="freeText18156317230361933182" style="display:none">Whenever I pick up a novel, I dive head first hopeful that the characters will have their happily ever afters. I picture their romance in my head like an endless reel of a silent movie: their first meeting will be perfectly awkward and the relationship to happen in a slow but realistic build-up that would have me anticipating and salivating for their fruition. But when the two characters wasn't really working so good for me, I'd also find myself wishing that they don't get together at all. This book may fall into the latter not because the two characters were an unlikable, unlikely couple but because I wanted to spare them the debilitating heartache that was to come. <br /><br />The book spans for what seems like a lifetime: two women who'd become friends and had gotten pregnant at the same time. Their kids grew up practically like twins. They can't seem to imagine their lives without one another. But as these stories go sometimes, people just drift apart. Or in their case, they were afraid to address how they really felt. Years go by, relationships falter and die but the one constant thing between these two kids is that big <b>what if</b>. Don't fret though, they would be given the chance. Readers would be given a moment or two to savour that sweet, joyful moment when they finally get together. Like rays of sunshine breaking from a persistent dark clouds and kids singing hallelujah in divine concurrence. But just as soon as it starts, the author will yank that little joy from you. All the while ripping your heart from the cavity of your chest with her bare hands. <br /><br />It's hard to get over something when you didn't understand what happened to begin with. I wasn't given the time to digest, ponder or even savour. And I can't figure out why I'm surprised because I already knew Phineas will die from the beginning. Hours after I closed the book, I'm still shell-shocked. It's not fair. I waited, the length of the entire novel for Finn and Autumn to get together. And then he dies. HE DIES. HE DIES. HE DIES. <br /><br />I'm so angry at this book. I wished I never read it. Which is stupid because it's one of the best, heart breaking novel I've ever read. So much so that I hugged the living shit out of it afterwards. In my head, I was imagining it was Autumn, doing my part at comforting her in her grief. If I were destroyed, then I can't even imagine the depths of her sorrow; of finally, finally being free to express the love that she's kept an entire lifetime only to drown in an ocean of misery afterwards. I said the exact thing to my husband, to which he replied: <br /><br /><i>"Honey, you do realize that this is a work of fiction, right?...and that none of those characters were real?"</i> <br /><br />But he doesn't understand. It's like Autumn when she finished writing her novel and she was overcome with grief over her characters. It's exactly how I felt. It's like they died and there wasn't a damn thing I can do about it. It's like I've known them my whole life when they've only spent an entire day inside my head. It's the hopelessness I feel and great black hole of knowing what happened was irreversible. I'm so deeply affected and I don't even know why. <br /><br />I wish y'all would read this book. I'm breathless and achy and I want to say exactly how I'm feeling but I'm a little short on words. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18156317230361933182" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review476810581">

<div id="review_452531017" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/452531017" />
    <a title="Sarah {Literary Meanderings}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4379747-sarah-literary-meanderings"><img alt="Sarah {Literary Meanderings}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552765806p2/4379747.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/452531017?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah {Literary Meanderings}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah {Literary Meanderings}" href="/user/show/4379747-sarah-literary-meanderings">Sarah {Literary Meanderings}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379747-sarah-literary-meanderings?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379747-sarah-literary-meanderings?shelf=tragedy-is-tragic">tragedy-is-tragic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379747-sarah-literary-meanderings?shelf=high-school">high-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379747-sarah-literary-meanderings?shelf=friendship-goals">friendship-goals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379747-sarah-literary-meanderings?shelf=title-appeal">title-appeal</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer452531017" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14106348677046370741"><br/>♥ Find my reviews here: <a href='http://www.literaryme.net/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Literary Meanderings</a><br/><br/>- - -<br/><br/><i>If He Had Been With Me</i> opens up to Autumn, our protagonist, thinking back to the fateful August night when her best friend Finny was involved in a tragic accident.<br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“They were arguing. No one ever says what they were arguing about. It is, in other people's opinions, not important to the story. What they do not know is that there is another story. The story lurking underneath and in between the facts of the one they can see. What they do not </i></b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText14106348677046370741" style="display:none"><br />♥ Find my reviews here: <a href="http://www.literaryme.net/" rel="nofollow noopener">Literary Meanderings</a><br /><br />- - -<br /><br /><i>If He Had Been With Me</i> opens up to Autumn, our protagonist, thinking back to the fateful August night when her best friend Finny was involved in a tragic accident.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“They were arguing. No one ever says what they were arguing about. It is, in other people's opinions, not important to the story. What they do not know is that there is another story. The story lurking underneath and in between the facts of the one they can see. What they do not know, the cause of the argument, is crucial to the story of me.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote>Then we backtrack to learn the story of Autumn and Phineas (aka Finny) from the very beginning.<br /><br />Their mothers (aka “The Mothers”) have been best friends for a very long time. They were pregnant at the same time and had their children within a week of each other. Naturally, Autumn and Finny grew up together. The two were inseparable. Autumn was always the oddball at school, but she always had Finny to watch over her and defend her honor.<br /><br />Until middle school. The two best friends grow apart after a misunderstanding that neither of them see (at the time) as a misunderstanding. While still in each others lives via family get-togethers with The Mothers, the two are merely cordial and polite—if anything, it's now an awkward not-quite-friendship. This continues through high school. Both teens are happily dating and have their separate social groups, etc.<br /><br />But Autumn has never stopped thinking of the “what ifs”... After battling with herself over it for some time, the question that remains is this: <i>Is it too late?</i><br /><br />Can what's been done be <i>undone</i>? Can friendship be like riding a bicycle? Can these two make their lives fit together after all these years?<br /><br />- - -<br /><br />First of all, I have to stick with my very first thought after reading this book: <b>Can I give this book a million stars?</b> Because it SO deserves that and more! Where do I even <i>begin</i>? How can I even <i>express</i> how much this book touched me; effected me? It has been a very very very long time since a book has made me cry so hard. It's something that I <i>crave</i> in a book. I want to <i>feel</i> the words in my mind, heart, and soul. Laura Nowlin has created a story that did this and <i>more</i>. It left me a complete freaking wreck! I had to sit on this review for over two weeks. I couldn't put it into words, and frankly, I'm still having trouble. I just want to scream it from the rooftops. <b>THIS BOOK IS AMAZING! IT WILL TAKE HOLD OF YOU FROM BEGINNING TO END!</b> <br /><br />Autumn and Finny. Oh, these two touched my heart so much! From the very start, their connection was tangible. Even when the two of them weren't really friends and didn't speak much, save perfunctory formalities. Through Autumn's first-person POV, we can see and feel their connection; their bond—a bond that transcends time.<br /><br />Autumn is one of the best protagonists I've ever met. I adored her personality and adored reading through her. She is quirky and artistic. She thinks things that you'd never quite expect of a high school girl. She doesn't care that she's different; she embraces it. She takes it and makes it her own. I am also thoroughly impressed with the very <i>REFRESHING</i> fact that Nowlin made this girl <u>confident</u>! She knows she is pretty and <i>says</i> so. She doesn't constantly doubt what she has to give or what she looks like. She doesn't have to. She is an inspiration! I think <i>everyone</i> who reads this book will just fall madly in love with her.<br /><br />Finny is someone we sort of see from afar. Through Autumn, we learn that he is slightly bashful, but has definite bold streak that rears it's head when needed. He's blonde, gorgeous, and a complete gentleman. He's also passionate, patient, and completely lovable. And love him I <i>soooo</i> did. Sigh.<br /><br />Nowlin's top-notch character development didn't stop with just Autumn and Finny. Their family was fully developed as were their friends. This book had <i>no</i> disposable or pointless characters. Each one was distinctly part of the story, and I'm finding this to be a rarity these days. It almost seems too <i>easy</i> to whip up a Young Adult novel and get it published. Throw in a vampire or a werewolf, a stupid girl who doesn't care about her own safety, and whammo! You're in like Flynn. This book, this author, seem the opposite to me. You can tell that she poured her heart and soul; pieces of herself, into this novel. Her writing is spectacular. Her words are poetic. This book will become a part of you.<br /><br />Now, from the blurb and the prologue of the novel, you already know a tragedy looms in the future. It's not something that surprises you. You know it's going to happen. Don't go into this book expecting your run-of-the-mill happy ending, because you won't get it. This book is <i>real</i> and it's <i>raw</i>. This isn't a paranormal tale where someone's beloved comes back from the dead, or even from the brink of death. It's inevitable, and you know this from the beginning. That being said, Nowlin was still able to stun me with the ending. I was still completely heartbroken and distraught when <i>
  <b>it</b>
</i> happened. The whole book is meant to make you grow to love these characters, to become a part of their life, and it worked 100%. I was fully invested in the outcome of this book, and the events hit me hard. I bawled through the last bit of chapters. I was a snotty, teary mess. I'm sort of glad my husband wasn't home. Although I did call him immediately after I finished to blab about the book for a good thirty minutes. About how much it touched me and how much I loved it. He dutifully gave me consolation over the phone. :) Anyway, I can promise you that this book will stay with you for the <i>rest of your life</i>.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I think we're supposed to experience as much beauty as we can.”<br /><br />“[...] because sometimes sad things are beautiful,” I say. “Like when someone dies.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote>All in all, I suppose it's needless to say that this book floored me. Heck, I'll say it anyway... <i>IF HE HAD BEEN WITH ME</i> FLOORED ME! Nowlin has staggering characterization skills, and a true talent for creating unique characters for readers to fall in love with. The plot is paced to perfection and you'll be turning the pages 'til the wee hours of the morning. This is definitely one of those “Just one more chapter!” books. The author soundly explores the relationship dynamics between childhood friends going through the transition of dealing with hormones and feelings they've never experienced, to the delicate beginnings of love. She gives us an ending that surprises even though it was foretold. Clever plot twists were woven into the story from the very beginning, making the ending one that packs a whole lot of punch. It's beautiful. It's sad. It's heart-wrenching.<br /><br />If you're looking for an emotionally-charged teen read, this is your book—hands down. Fans of YA Contemporary Romance, New Adult, or Coming of Age will also enjoy this book. It does touch on some rough subjects: teen pregnancy, underage drinking, suicide, sex, etc. It's done tastefully and with respect. Just do yourself a favor and go out and buy this book or pick it up at the library. Autumn and Finny's story is one that will stay with you forever and ever. Be warned, though! This book requires a bit of recovery time after you finish up. :)<br /><br />- - -<br /><br /><b>Book source:</b> <a href="https://www.netgalley.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">NetGalley</a><br /><b>Publisher:</b> Sourcebooks Fire/Sourcebooks<br /></span>

<div id="review_585487938" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/585487938" />
    <a title="Devyani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6250148-devyani"><img alt="Devyani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438017713p2/6250148.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/585487938?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Devyani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Devyani" href="/user/show/6250148-devyani">Devyani</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6250148-devyani?shelf=moved-my-soul">moved-my-soul</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer585487938" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13972927704505025269">It’s a pattern. <br/><br/>Every time around this time of the year, I find myself drifting away from my reading and reviewing obsession. It’s not because I want to. It’s because circumstances around me eventually make me. It’s the start of summer here. And there are SO MANY things to do! There are those annual fests and functions to be part of. Lots of camping to do. Lots of catching up to do with my family and there is lots of travelling. Amidst it all, my reading just falls behind and then I don’t even f</span>
  <span id="freeText13972927704505025269" style="display:none">It’s a pattern. <br /><br />Every time around this time of the year, I find myself drifting away from my reading and reviewing obsession. It’s not because I want to. It’s because circumstances around me eventually make me. It’s the start of summer here. And there are SO MANY things to do! There are those annual fests and functions to be part of. Lots of camping to do. Lots of catching up to do with my family and there is lots of travelling. Amidst it all, my reading just falls behind and then I don’t even feel like reviewing. BUT THIS BOOK.<br /><br />It makes me stay up late at night and just type, type, type and type.<br /><br />Let me just warn you all. This review is pathetically nonsensical because it was written right after I finished reading this book. And the initial reaction to a book is pure emotion and it <i>always</i> does not make sense. So you’re free to run away and totally ignore this review.<br /><br />I’m just happy. I’m just so so happy. I could almost cry happy tears. And no, it’s not because of something that happened in the book but it’s because of the effect it had on me. I love those moments of gut wrenching metaphorical pain where you just want to punch something so bad and just howl and wail and cry and jhinga-la-la-la dance around a bonfire like a mad man in the middle of a ritual and throw yourself into that burning bonfire because after what happened in the book , you are never going to be the same. I love those moments of earthquakes that rock my heart because as sadist authors intended, you as a reader know what exactly the end is going to be and you just don’t want to read the damn end as much you truly need to because you know it’s going to tear you apart even though you already know what happens from the very beginning of the damn book. <br /><br />I’ve read better books. I think. <br /><br />And there will be times when books written by great minds will appear at my doorstep or just my laptop or kindle and would make me want to die of ecstasy or just ecstatic pain. If that makes sense. Among those many books will be a few that even after being replaced by another set of books , will never truly leave your mind and will always linger. This book is one of those.<br /><br /><b>If he had been with me</b> by Laura Nowlin is a very simple book with a very simple yet captivating writing style. The pace is perfect and so is every angle and every mood. <br />It was heart breaking , stomach bursting , mind blasting , ground shaking , sky tearing and just about every term of destruction with an ‘–ing’ at the end of it. <br /><br />Maybe I’m just overreacting. But guess what? I don’t care. Because I’m a very very very VERY happy person. I’m heartbroken but I’m very satisfied. <br />I got what I wanted from this book. To be honest, I was expecting a more ....I don’t know how to say it...but er, a more dramatic end?<br />I mean hey, it was by all means pure awesomeness but I just wanted something more. But like I said earlier, I’m a satisfied reader and now when I rationally think about it, I feel that it’s good that the things ended the way they did. <br /><br />I’m in no position to talk about the characters. I can only just tell you this. I hate the reality that were both, Autumn and Finn. <br />I hate how real situation was. I hate the damn title. ‘I he had been with me’ : I’m going to punch somebody. <br />I just...I was so frustrated at times. And then I was sad. And then I was happy and then I was sad again. Then I was happy and it just went on and on and on. I hate the last line of this damn book. <br /><br />Come to think of it?<br /><br />I HATE THIS BOOK.<br /><br />Shoo. I don’t want to think about Finn. Especially Finny. Because he was something every girl dreams of . Not because he was a total hottaaay (which btw he was.) and not because he was a champion at wooing a girl. No. Nada. Niet. <br />He was awkward. And I loved how he loved people. He wasn’t perfect but he was something. His character was so real! Not every guy is a cocky I-know-you-want-me-and-you-know-I-want-you kind of a guy who has that sexy half smirk always on his face. And who has a Adonis like body and is totally badass. Not every guy is sensitive. Nobody is perfect. And Finn is not perfect. But when you read about him you know that there is something absolutely right about this beautiful boy. <br /><br />Autumn? <br />Insecure ? Dreamer? Teenager? Confused? Afraid? Needy? Loved? Alone?<br />I still can’t find the right words to explain how I feel about her . I just know that she was a good narrator. And that I enjoyed the ride. <br /><br />Okay. I love this book. <br /><br />Bye you all.<br /><br />I’m sure you know what to do. <br /><br />You can make me happy by reading this book. And be happy yourself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13972927704505025269" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_561790115" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/561790115" />
    <a title="Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3399699-rose"><img alt="Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386022874p2/3399699.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/561790115?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/3399699-rose">Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=grief">grief</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=tough-subjects">tough-subjects</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=psychological">psychological</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer561790115" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9676842510950666810"><b>Pre-read:</b> I'm so happy I was approved for the galley of this, looking forward to reading it. Also, look at the cover! o_O It's beautiful.<br/><br/><b>Post-read:</b> Solid read, if a bit fragmented in places. I liked Autumn's journey, even if I had an idea of how most things would happen.<br/><br/><b>Full review:</b><br/><br/>"If He Had Been With Me" is a journey that's immersed around a tragedy, and that's something you get from point one in this book by Laura Nowlin. It surprised me how it drew me into the narrative even when I knew how </span>
  <span id="freeText9676842510950666810" style="display:none"><b>Pre-read:</b> I'm so happy I was approved for the galley of this, looking forward to reading it. Also, look at the cover! o_O It's beautiful.<br /><br /><b>Post-read:</b> Solid read, if a bit fragmented in places. I liked Autumn's journey, even if I had an idea of how most things would happen.<br /><br /><b>Full review:</b><br /><br />"If He Had Been With Me" is a journey that's immersed around a tragedy, and that's something you get from point one in this book by Laura Nowlin. It surprised me how it drew me into the narrative even when I knew how things would turn out as the story unfolded, but the emotional clarity and resonance is solid throughout, which makes it a strong read in the measure of grief, coming of age, and coping. <br /><br />Autumn and Finn were neighbors and close friends growing up, until a respective falling out distanced them over time. The narrative here follows Autumn through high school and a little beyond graduation. Autumn has her own relationship with Jamie, while Finn has his relationship with Sylvie. The narrative goes through their respective life events, covering four years of high school, a little bit after that, and certain turning points in their past and present from Autumn's perspective. Even when I knew what would eventually happen, I enjoyed watching the journey of this novel because of the emotional clarity and coherence in Autumn's perspective. She was well worth following. I did think there was a bit of a distance in the narrative in some points with some roughness in transition with respect to the time jumps, but in terms of it being a story of grief, it was a good one. <br /><br />The collective cast of characters here felt very realistic and drawn well in their interactions with each other. I think the only part I found myself struggling with more towards the end was somewhat of the jumping point in the aftermath of the tragedy - almost like it could've gone a little further in terms of resolution, though it gives some note of Autumn attempting to come to terms with things. I enjoyed it and certainly wouldn't hesitate to read more from Nowlin in the future.<br /><br />Overall score: 3.5/5 stars<br /><br />Note: I received this as an ARC from NetGalley, from the publisher.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9676842510950666810" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Now some of the issues I can't help but be "ugh, get over it", "hahahahha, together in complete love and happiness from freshman year to forever" (I know it happens don't @ me), and just the general over indulgence, and scared of the newness, are kind of missed by me.<br /><br />This is all first person from the heroine which is also hard for me because I like insight from other characters. The writing is captivating at times but manipulated emotion isn't real to me, boys and babies don't cure depression or act as a cure all, and I missed having a pov from Finn. <div id="review_575889837" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/575889837" />
    <a title="Aly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3646617-aly"><img alt="Aly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1332091516p2/3646617.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/575889837?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aly" href="/user/show/3646617-aly">Aly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3646617-aly?shelf=2013-ya-contempt">2013-ya-contempt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3646617-aly?shelf=e-arc">e-arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer575889837" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13225749595693394149">I had such a visceral and emotionally charged reaction to this book. I wish my vocabulary was enough to sufficient describe how amazing this book was, I wish I had the power of persuasion that could convince the most reluctant readers to give If He Had Been With Me a chance...and I guess this review will have to suffice. <br/><br/>"Sometimes sad things are beautiful"<br/><br/>This sentence not only perfectly describes this novel, but also my experience reading it. By the end, I was in tears, a huge emotionally wrec</span>
  <span id="freeText13225749595693394149" style="display:none">I had such a visceral and emotionally charged reaction to this book. I wish my vocabulary was enough to sufficient describe how amazing this book was, I wish I had the power of persuasion that could convince the most reluctant readers to give If He Had Been With Me a chance...and I guess this review will have to suffice. <br /><br />"Sometimes sad things are beautiful"<br /><br />This sentence not only perfectly describes this novel, but also my experience reading it. By the end, I was in tears, a huge emotionally wreck, but at the same time, I was glad. I mean I connected with the book in a way that completely took me by surprise, I fell in love with the cover and the premise, but that doesn't necessarily make for a good book. From the very first page, though, Nowlin, captured my attention. I knew this story wouldn't have a happy ending, but every time I turned the page, I hoped that I was wrong and a miracle would occur. <br /><br />Finny and Autumn were inseparable as children, but as they grew up they grew apart. For years they have been living separate lives, that weren't really as divided as they seemed. Finny has always been there for Autumn, and after graduation they are finally able to fully rehabilitate their friendship and maybe begin something more...<br /><br />Nowlin is a crafter of words and characters. Her character development is simply genius and her words are like a Polaroid camera that captures the personalities of her characters. Her characters don't simply live within the pages of this novel, they are extremely realistic. They are so complex and it's too easy to let them in, befriend them, know them. Her words are like magic. There are so many moments in the novel where I had to stop because I just felt so connected with her words, the characters, and the situations that Nowlin has created. <br /><br />Nowlin's writing is John Green-esque and fans of The Fault in Our Stars will surely love this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13225749595693394149" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer3189762454693156459"><br/>Finny, the all star soccer player, and Autumn, the artistic sensitive soul, have always been connected. To outsiders, this couple seem as mismatched as a Capulet and a Montague. As many in their world judge them by appearances, Nowlin subtly introduces her audience to two souls growing together with intertwined lives that defy traditional stereotypes. Raised by "The Mothers" with absentee fathers in neighboring houses, Finny and Autumn resist natural boundaries that normally separate friends fro</span>
  <span id="freeText3189762454693156459" style="display:none"><br />Finny, the all star soccer player, and Autumn, the artistic sensitive soul, have always been connected. To outsiders, this couple seem as mismatched as a Capulet and a Montague. As many in their world judge them by appearances, Nowlin subtly introduces her audience to two souls growing together with intertwined lives that defy traditional stereotypes. Raised by "The Mothers" with absentee fathers in neighboring houses, Finny and Autumn resist natural boundaries that normally separate friends from family.<br /> <br />We delve deeper into their lives with the start of ninth grade. Remember High School? Not the high school you remember through rose colored glasses, but the real thing. The complicated, annoying, derisive challenges that keep cliques alive and stereotypes thriving. Nowlin shines here as she showcases the true high school experience, not a "glee-esque" facade. Various complications test the relationships of characters as we experience these four years with Nowlin's fully expressed cast. Even supporting characters have fully actualized personalities and story lines.This is especially refreshing after reading other teen novels. No disposable characters here. Nowlin has no paranormal crutch or distopian future to hide behind. As we watch these years come to an end, Nowlin transitions easily in to post-high school life. She fluidly shows how those barriers fall away in favor of relationships as characters grow out of their old lives and into new ones. Her characters begin to make up their own minds, setting out on their own paths. Nowlin's subtle plot twists lead us to an unexpected and dramatic conclusion. The delicate use of foreshadowing pops up occasionally, leading the reader down a path that is both beautiful and tragic. We know where we are going, but it is still a shock when we get there. <br /> <br />"If He Had Been With Me" is quite an experience. It is, as Autumn would say, a beautifully sad thing. If you're looking for a teen novel with surprising depth and emotional impact, this one is for you. The interweaving of the familial problems of divorce, depression, and expectations combined with the normal drama of high school take this novel to the "next level." With a debut like this, I can't wait to read Laura Nowlin's next novel. I'm just not sure if I'll find it in the teen section or if she'll take the leap to adult fiction. Based on writing like this, she's definitely ready to cater to both audiences.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3189762454693156459" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_567172884" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/567172884" />
    <a title="Proserpine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5485420-proserpine"><img alt="Proserpine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1335559519p2/5485420.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Proserpine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Proserpine" href="/user/show/5485420-proserpine">Proserpine</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9009885499976725358">OMG!<br/><br/>Ouff! I'm still recovering from this story! Sometime, you'll get the chance (just like me) to read a book that will mark you for the rest of the day, year, life. If He Had Been With Me, is one of those books I will never forget for many good and unexpected reasons, but still, this story hold a special place on my shelve: the Keeper shelve.<br/><br/>There's a lot a good and great books out there, but this one is stand out. The cover is beautiful and intriguing, but the blurb is the thing that had catch</span>
  <span id="freeText9009885499976725358" style="display:none">OMG!<br /><br />Ouff! I'm still recovering from this story! Sometime, you'll get the chance (just like me) to read a book that will mark you for the rest of the day, year, life. If He Had Been With Me, is one of those books I will never forget for many good and unexpected reasons, but still, this story hold a special place on my shelve: the Keeper shelve.<br /><br />There's a lot a good and great books out there, but this one is stand out. The cover is beautiful and intriguing, but the blurb is the thing that had catch my attention. March and April are two busy months for me this year, but I wanted to read this book so bad that even if I knew I didn't have the time to do it, I wanted, I needed to read this one. I had a presentiment and I didn't even read early reviews because I wanted to make up my mind on my own.<br /><br />This book haunted me for hours after I have finished it, I'm still thinking about it. Laura Nowlin have been writing a wonderful story about childhood love growing into something more, something special, but also something scary. This story is about two friends that shared more than love and almost lost everything. How hard life can be when you denied yourself from what you want you really need. This book is about how beautiful life can be, about how you fight your way out and survives and finally how destiny always wins.<br /><br />We got two very different characters: Finny and Autumn (oh, I love that name!). They are inseparable as the blurb says and one day, something happened and the reader will be enticed in this story right after this fateful moment.<br /><br />What if? Always the same unanswered question. The author Laura Nowlin (that I will now call: one of my favorite super awesome author Laura Nolin :D) has given us a very personal and fabulous story that won't leave your mind for a time. Her writing style was easy, flowing and inviting.<br /><br />I loved Autumn, I got attached to her easily. Doing her thing, but still anchored into her own world. Her imagination, creativity and writing are what make her wake up in the morning. She's the weirdo, but could pass unnoticed too, just like me in high school!<br /><br />Finny is the kind of guy that I would have fall in love with in high school. He's the handsome guy but he doesn't care. Every girl want him, but he knows better than to play the show-off. Is the kind of sexy and shy geek next door?<br /><br />This story brought me a range of raw emotion inside of me. This one is a real tear-jerker! I wasn’t able to stop reading and I was eager to go home after work to read a few chapters, a few pages, dawn just a few lines was all I need to be at ease! This book is about possibility, but still, it's a reminder of what life got in store and no matter what, you can't go back in time. You have to go through life.<br /> <br />Page Turner: Yes!<br /><br />Series: No<br /><br />Stand Alone: Yes<br /><br />Hotness: Hmmm, Finny of course! But this book isn't about hot and sexy male!<br /><br />Proserpine Recommendation: This book is a must-read, a must-try a must-everything I need to say for you to pick it up and try it! If you like Contemporary Romance, New Adult Romance, If He Had Been With Me should be on your top Next-To-Buy list!<br />BUY-BORROW, do something!!!!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9009885499976725358" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Eve" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12014819-eve"><img alt="Eve" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550055795p2/12014819.jpg" /></a>
